 delete loadQueue;

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

          width: 100%;

          padding-top: 0.5em;
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Externally reported security bugs may appear in Chrome release notes. If



<b class="line"><!---->Externally reported security bugs may appear in Chrome release notes. If<!----></b>

this bug is included, how would you like to be credited?



<b class="line"><!---->this bug is included, how would you like to be credited?<!----></b>

Reporter credit: Alan Goodman



<span class="line"><!---->Reporter credit: Alan Goodman<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is a bit of a peculiar report; so much so that I almost did not bother to report this.  However after browsing around v8 dcheck related reports I've seen other extremely hard to reproduce crashes get fixed and actually be important problems.  Therefore I present to you a trace I keep running into while fuzzing using v8_wasm_compile_fuzzer.  It always occurs while doing the initial corpus load at the start of the fuzz processes life and typially between step 4096 and 16384.  On a cluster with 112 real cores; running 112 processes and starting with attached corpus I will typically see a crash like above within the first hour (usually multiple times).  It seems to crash on a different corpus file each time and I've ran a selection of the files in infinite loops; with different system load conditions without reproducing anything.  However as I previously stated I can reproduce this 100% of the time within one hour simply by starting the fuzzing session.  As fuzz instances die and get respawned I will see more and more instances of this crash.  As ever; I hope you find this report useful.



<span class="line"><!---->This is a bit of a peculiar report; so much so that I almost did not bother to report this.  However after browsing around v8 dcheck related reports I've seen other extremely hard to reproduce crashes get fixed and actually be important problems.  Therefore I present to you a trace I keep running into while fuzzing using v8_wasm_compile_fuzzer.  It always occurs while doing the initial corpus load at the start of the fuzz processes life and typially between step 4096 and 16384.  On a cluster with 112 real cores; running 112 processes and starting with attached corpus I will typically see a crash like above within the first hour (usually multiple times).  It seems to crash on a different corpus file each time and I've ran a selection of the files in infinite loops; with different system load conditions without reproducing anything.  However as I previously stated I can reproduce this 100% of the time within one hour simply by starting the fuzzing session.  As fuzz instances die and get respawned I will see more and more instances of this crash.  As ever; I hope you find this report useful.<!----></span>

 since both these crashes would be explained by double-initialization of external pointer slots.

Looking at the stacktrace, this line from the stacktrace might already be enough to figure out the issue:



<span class="line"><!---->Looking at the stacktrace, this line from the stacktrace might already be enough to figure out the issue:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





    #16 0x557ff6636254 in v8::internal::MarkingVisitorBase<v8::internal::ConcurrentMarkingVisitor>::VisitJSArrayBuffer(v8::internal::Tagged<v8::internal::Map>, v8::internal::Tagged<v8::internal::JSArrayBuffer>) ../../v8/src/heap/marking-visitor-inl.h:501:10



<span class="line"><!---->    #16 0x557ff6636254 in v8::internal::MarkingVisitorBase&lt;v8::internal::ConcurrentMarkingVisitor&gt;::VisitJSArrayBuffer(v8::internal::Tagged&lt;v8::internal::Map&gt;, v8::internal::Tagged&lt;v8::internal::JSArrayBuffer&gt;) ../../v8/src/heap/marking-visitor-inl.h:501:10<!----></span>

This would indicate that some external pointer slot of a JSArrayBuffer is written to twice. This could be double-initialization, but, thinking about it again, it could also be this here: 



<span class="line"><!---->This would indicate that some external pointer slot of a JSArrayBuffer is written to twice. This could be double-initialization, but, thinking about it again, it could also be this here: <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:v8/src/objects/js-array-buffer-inl.h;l=127;drc=f4fc9e05f6931668879d7f0a90fe4dcf564f2d59



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:v8/src/objects/js-array-buffer-inl.h;l=127;drc=f4fc9e05f6931668879d7f0a90fe4dcf564f2d59"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:v8/src/objects/js-array-buffer-inl.h;l=127;drc=f4fc9e05f6931668879d7f0a90fe4dcf564f2d59<!----></a>





 in that case, we'd write zero into the slot, which is allowed but would confuse the DCHECK (so in that case, just this DCHECK would be wrong).



<span class="line"><!----> in that case, we'd write zero into the slot, which is allowed but would confuse the DCHECK (so in that case, just this DCHECK would be wrong).<!----></span>

Thanks for testing! Ah yeah I think you're right, you're probably running a non-debug (is_debug=false) but dcheck-enabled build (usually DCHECKs are only enabled in debug builds, but you can set e.g. dcheck_always_on=true, and maybe use_libfuzzer=true also enables them). Could you try again without the #ifdef and #endif? Sorry for the trouble!



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for testing! Ah yeah I think you're right, you're probably running a non-debug (is_debug=false) but dcheck-enabled build (usually DCHECKs are only enabled in debug builds, but you can set e.g. dcheck_always_on=true, and maybe use_libfuzzer=true also enables them). Could you try again without the #ifdef and #endif? Sorry for the trouble!<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->In any case I'll also prepare a CL to fix that DCHECK, since it looks wrong in any case.<!----></span>

Wonderful, thanks! I've prepared a fix: 



<span class="line"><!---->Wonderful, thanks! I've prepared a fix: <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/4898680



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/4898680"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/4898680<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





In that case, it's not double-initialization (which leads to suboptimal behavior of the compaction algorithm but no correctness/security impact) but "de-initialization" (where an external pointer slot is set to the null handle). This happens when a JSArrayBuffer is detached, as its external pointer to the Extension object is then cleared. This is fine, but our DCHECKs didn't expect it, basically.



<span class="line"><!---->In that case, it's not double-initialization (which leads to suboptimal behavior of the compaction algorithm but no correctness/security impact) but "de-initialization" (where an external pointer slot is set to the null handle). This happens when a JSArrayBuffer is detached, as its external pointer to the Extension object is then cleared. This is fine, but our DCHECKs didn't expect it, basically.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Thanks again for reporting and testing the fix!



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks again for reporting and testing the fix!<!----></span>

          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
